Muzzleloading Shotguns (1) -

Comply With Muzzleloader Specifications For Turkey Hunting In Washington State
Reference Source: wdfw01803
Procedure:

1. Ensure the muzzleloader is legal for turkey hunting in Washington State by meeting these criteria:
- It must be a firearm loaded from the muzzle using black powder or a black powder substitute.
- The firearm must be...
Procedure:

1. Ensure the muzzleloader is legal for turkey hunting in Washington State by meeting these criteria:
- It must be a firearm loaded from the muzzle using black powder or a black powder substitute.
- The firearm must be considered loaded if it contains a powder charge and projectile (shot or single projectile), with the barrel or breech capped or primed.
- The muzzleloading shotgun must have a single or double barrel.
- It must shoot #4 or smaller shot when used for turkey hunting.
- Persons hunting small game may keep both barrels of a double-barrel, muzzleloading shotgun loaded.

2. Use only black powder or a black powder substitute rated for your specific muzzleloader model to avoid dangerous malfunctions.

3. Follow safety practices:
- Never fill the muzzleloader directly from the powder can as it may spark and ignite the powder in the can.
- Mark the ramrod when the muzzleloader is empty so you can confirm it is empty during storage.
- Ensure the wad and shot are seated directly on top of the powder charge.
- Store powder and percussion caps separately, in dry, cool places.

4. Be aware of a hang fire: if the trigger is pulled and the firearm does not discharge within 30 seconds, keep the muzzle pointed in a safe direction for at least 30 seconds. If it still does not fire, put on another cap or re-prime the pan, then fire again.

5. Ensure the nipple is clean on percussion locks to avoid misfires.
muzzleloader, turkey hunting, black powder, safety, legal requirements, hang fire

Clothing Selection (1) -

Layer Clothing for Temperature Regulation During Hunting
Standard Source: wdfw01803
Dressing in Layers for Comfort and Efficiency:

1. Assess the Activity and Weather Conditions:
- For hiking or physically demanding tasks, wear fewer layers to allow for easier movement.
- When setting up at a hunting spot and sitting...
Dressing in Layers for Comfort and Efficiency:

1. Assess the Activity and Weather Conditions:
- For hiking or physically demanding tasks, wear fewer layers to allow for easier movement.
- When setting up at a hunting spot and sitting for extended periods, add more layers for warmth.

2. Use Layering Techniques:
- Start with a moisture-wicking base layer (e.g., synthetic or wool).
- Add an insulating mid-layer (e.g., fleece or down) for warmth in cold conditions.
- Finish with a waterproof and windproof outer shell to protect against the elements.

3. Protective Outerwear:
- Consider wearing tough jeans or brush pants when working in dense vegetation to prevent scratches and abrasions.
- Ensure all layers are breathable to avoid overheating and sweating.
layering,hunting,clothing,temperature regulation

Camouflage Selection (1) -

Choose Camouflage Clothing Based on Habitat and Climate
Standard Source: wdfw01803
Selecting Effective Camouflage Patterns:

1. Match Camouflage to the Environment:
- Use all-purpose camouflage patterns if unsure of where you will be hunting.
- For specific habitats (e.g., forest, grassland), choose patterns that...
Selecting Effective Camouflage Patterns:

1. Match Camouflage to the Environment:
- Use all-purpose camouflage patterns if unsure of where you will be hunting.
- For specific habitats (e.g., forest, grassland), choose patterns that match the colors and textures of the terrain.

2. Avoid Contrasting Patterns in Inappropriate Environments:
- Do not use waterfowl camo when hunting turkeys in timber areas; it will make you more visible.
- Opt for natural color schemes (green, brown, black) that blend with the surrounding landscape if unsure.

3. Conceal Facial and Hand Features:
- Use face paint or a face covering to break up your facial outline and avoid detection by animals.
- Wear gloves in camouflage colors to match the rest of your clothing.

4. Invest in Purpose-Built Gear:
- Consider purchasing a turkey vest with a built-in seat cushion for comfort during long sits.
- Ensure all camo clothing is warm and waterproof, especially in the wet climate of the Pacific Northwest.
camouflage,hunting,habitat,concealment

Title: Submit a Hunter Report Online

Procedure:
1. Go to [fishhunt.dfw.wa.gov](http://fishhunt.dfw.wa.gov).
2. Under the “I want to Submit” section on the left-hand side (Highlighted in Orange), select “Hunter Report”.
3. Select the “Submit Report” box in the top-left corner of the page.
4. Enter all customer information fields and click “GO”.
5. If an error occurs, such as “Customer not found, please try your search again,” verify the information entered and correct it if necessary.
6. Select the first species under the “Choose a tag to report on:” section.
7. Answer all questions that appear on the screen. The questions will change based on the answers provided.
8. When completed, the report will issue a message stating, “You have finished the hunter report. Click FINISH to save all of your answers.” Click “FINISH” when completed.
9. A confirmation page will appear showing that the report has been submitted successfully.
10. Write down the submittal date and the confirmation number; this information may need to be referenced at a future date.
11. Use the Back button on the screen to return to the page that shows which tags need to be reported or have already been reported.
12. Repeat the process for all tags with an outstanding report.

Notes:
• This information is used by WDFW to set future hunting seasons in conjunction with field staff population surveys.
• If you encounter difficulties using the online system, you can also call 877-945-3492 and report by phone.
• Reporting is mandatory for all tags purchased except cougar. Failure to report by January 31 may result in a $10 administrative penalty.

Scouting Techniques (1) -

Scout for Elk in New Hunting Areas
Reference Source: wdfw01807
Procedure:

1. Cover Ground Thoroughly:
- Walk or drive through the area to locate signs of elk activity such as tracks, scat, and feeding areas.
- Pay special attention to roads and landings where fresh tracks may be visible...
Procedure:

1. Cover Ground Thoroughly:
- Walk or drive through the area to locate signs of elk activity such as tracks, scat, and feeding areas.
- Pay special attention to roads and landings where fresh tracks may be visible (especially on non-graveled surfaces).

2. Identify Key Areas:
- Focus on stands that provide cover and are adjacent to clearcuts or other open areas.
- Look for areas with abundant elk sign, which indicates high elk presence.

3. Use Topographic Maps:
- Later in the season, consult a topographic map to locate “benches” in steep terrain with thick cover.
- These benches are often used by elk as daytime bedding areas.

4. Access Restricted Areas:
- If non-motorized access is allowed, do not be deterred by locked gates.
- These areas may have less hunting pressure and could hold elk that are easier to hunt.
elk scouting,hunting techniques,new area exploration,topographic maps,bench identification

Elk Hunting Techniques (1) -

Locate Rocky Mountain Elk Using High Ridge Glassing
Standard Source: wdfw01807
Procedure:

1. Position yourself on a high ridge to gain an elevated vantage point.
2. Use glassing equipment (binoculars or spotting scope) to scan the area for elk herds.
3. Time your observation at first light, as elk typically...
Procedure:

1. Position yourself on a high ridge to gain an elevated vantage point.
2. Use glassing equipment (binoculars or spotting scope) to scan the area for elk herds.
3. Time your observation at first light, as elk typically begin feeding right after sunrise, increasing your chances of locating them.
4. Note the elk's behavior and movements once located, such as grazing patterns or herd dynamics.
5. Begin hiking toward the general area where the elk were spotted, preparing to employ a specific hunting technique based on terrain and conditions.
6. Be prepared for increased movement into remote areas due to hunting pressure, which may require leaving roads behind and venturing into backcountry locations.
7. Ensure you have a plan for transporting the elk back to your vehicle after a successful hunt.
elk hunting, glassing, high ridge, first light, tracking elk, hunting pressure, backcountry hunting

Archery Regulations (1) -

Comply with Archery Hunting Regulations in Washington State
Standard Source: wdfw01807
Procedure:

1. Use Legal Broadheads:
- Mechanical broadheads are legal for all archery hunting.
- Ensure that the broadhead blade or blades are at least seven eighths inch (7/8") wide.

2. Prohibited Items During Archery Season:
...
Procedure:

1. Use Legal Broadheads:
- Mechanical broadheads are legal for all archery hunting.
- Ensure that the broadhead blade or blades are at least seven eighths inch (7/8") wide.

2. Prohibited Items During Archery Season:
- It is unlawful to carry or have in possession any firearm while field archery hunting during an archery season, except for modern handguns carried for personal protection.
- Modern handguns cannot be used to hunt big game or dispatch wounded big game during an archery season.
- Electrical equipment or electric devices (except illuminated nocks) are prohibited on the bow or arrow while hunting.

3. Prohibited Actions:
- It is unlawful to shoot a bow and arrow from a vehicle, across, or along the maintained portion of a public highway.
- It is unlawful to use any device secured to or supported by the bow for maintaining it at full draw or in a firing position.

4. Bow Specifications:
- Bows must produce a minimum of 40 pounds of pull measured at twenty-eight inches or less draw length.
- Arrows used for hunting big game must be at least 20 inches in length and weigh no less than 6 grains per pound of draw weight, with a minimum arrow weight of 300 grains.

5. Scope Prohibition:
- It is unlawful to hunt wildlife with any bow equipped with a scope.

6. Crossbow Usage:
- Crossbows can be used during archery season only if the hunter is disabled and has been approved for a special use permit through WDFW’s ADA program.
- Refer to the crossbow information in the Modern Firearm Equipment section, as it is considered a modern firearm for hunting purposes.
archery,hunting regulations,broadhead requirements,WDFW,crossbow usage

Field Skills (1) -

Using Wind Indicators to Determine Wind Direction for Hunting Elk
Standard Source: wdfw01807
Materials Needed:
• Powder in a squeeze bottle (smoke indicator)
• Dry grass

Steps:
1. Use Smoke Indicator: Squeeze the powder from the bottle to release a puff of smoke. Observe how the smoke drifts; this will indicate the direction of...
Materials Needed:
• Powder in a squeeze bottle (smoke indicator)
• Dry grass

Steps:
1. Use Smoke Indicator: Squeeze the powder from the bottle to release a puff of smoke. Observe how the smoke drifts; this will indicate the direction of the wind.
2. Use Dry Grass Method: Pick up some dry grass and drop it from about eye height. The direction in which the grass falls indicates the wind direction.
3. Position Blind or Stand: Use the determined wind direction to position your blind or tree stand so that the wind is blowing toward you (in your face) for optimal concealment and detection of elk.
wind direction,hunting elk,smoke indicator,grass method

Optics (1) -

Selecting Quality Optics for Elk Hunting
Reference Source: wdfw01807
Selecting Quality Optics for Elk Hunting

• Understand optic designations: Optics have a designation like 8 x 42, where the first number (8) represents magnification and the second number (42) is the diameter of the objective lens in...
Selecting Quality Optics for Elk Hunting

• Understand optic designations: Optics have a designation like 8 x 42, where the first number (8) represents magnification and the second number (42) is the diameter of the objective lens in millimeters.
• Magnification impact: Higher magnification allows for viewing distant objects more clearly but may reduce image stability when handheld.
• Objective lens size: A larger objective lens (e.g., 42mm) allows more light to enter, resulting in a clearer and brighter image. However, larger lenses can make the optic bulkier.
• Test optics before purchasing: Visit a sporting goods store and test various models to determine which best suits your needs.
• Avoid using rifle scopes for glassing: Using a rifle scope to look through areas (glassing) is not recommended because it aligns the barrel with where you are looking, potentially compromising safety.
optics,magnification,objecive lens,hunting

Calls (1) -

Using Elk Calls in Washington
Standard Source: wdfw01807
Using Elk Calls in Washington

• Types of calls used:
- Bull bugle: Used to locate bull elk and is a challenge call for other bulls.
- Cow call: Used to attract bulls once they are located or to calm spooked herds by mimicking...
Using Elk Calls in Washington

• Types of calls used:
- Bull bugle: Used to locate bull elk and is a challenge call for other bulls.
- Cow call: Used to attract bulls once they are located or to calm spooked herds by mimicking cow sounds.
- Calf call: Similar to cow calls but higher pitched, used as a locator call for cows.
• Call usage tips:
- Avoid making quick cow calls, as the “bark” of an elk can signal danger and alert them to your presence.
- All calls (except push calls) require air movement to function properly.
• Push call:
- Used by pressing a plunger or air sack to move air over the reed.
- Ideal for making cow and calf calls.
- Great for beginners because it produces consistent sounds when activated.
• Diaphragm call:
- The most difficult to master, as it requires using your mouth to produce sound.
- Frees up hands for other tasks like aiming at a rutting bull.
- Requires significant practice; keep the call in your car to practice while driving.
• Bugle tube:
- Mimics a bugling bull and is used to locate herds, especially when trying to attract bulls that may be protecting cows.
- Can come with or without a diaphragm reed. If it doesn’t have one, purchase one from a store.
• Cow call (mouth-operated):
- Mimics cow sounds by placing your mouth over a reed and blowing gently.
- Similar to a duck call in design.
elk calls,bull bugle,cow call,calf call,push call,diaphragm call,bugle tube

Tracking Skills (1) -

Tracking a Wounded Animal
Standard Source: wdfw01807
Tracking a Wounded Animal

• Tracking is one of the most difficult skills to learn, but it's essential for retrieving big game.
• If an animal runs off after being shot, you must follow the blood trail to find it.
• Give the animal about 30...
Tracking a Wounded Animal

• Tracking is one of the most difficult skills to learn, but it's essential for retrieving big game.
• If an animal runs off after being shot, you must follow the blood trail to find it.
• Give the animal about 30 minutes after the shot to lie down and expire. Watch and listen for any indications that the animal may be down.
• Go to the spot where the animal was standing at the time of impact.
• If there are two hunters, have one stay at the shooting position and the other go to the impact spot.
• Look for blood or hair in the immediate area. Examine the blood:
- Bubbly blood indicates a shot to the lungs.
- Dark red blood indicates a heart shot.
- Black blood indicates a liver shot.
• If you are an archer, look at the arrow for clues about the type of hit.
• Slowly make your way toward the last place you saw the elk running, keeping your eyes on the ground and sweeping left to right for more blood.
• If no blood is found, walk in slow circles until you see more sign. Use lighted tools at night if available.
• Mark the spot of the last blood or have one hunter stay there while the other makes a slow circle about 10 feet away.
• If no blood is found at 10 feet, adjust your distance accordingly.
• This process should be slow and methodical.
• Continue tracking until you find the animal.
• If you hear the animal rise and run off again, wait another 30 minutes before continuing the tracking effort.
• When you find the animal, approach it from behind to verify that it has expired. This can be done by gently poking the animal with a stick or hunting equipment.
• If the animal is not dead, dispatch it as humanely as possible.
tracking wounded animal, blood trail, hunting techniques

Legal Requirements (1) -

Tagging a Harvested Big Game Animal
Reference Source: wdfw01807
Tagging a Harvested Big Game Animal

• Immediately after killing any big game animal, the appropriate tag must be validated.
• Cut out and completely remove the month and day of kill from the tag. A slit is not acceptable.
• Securely attach...
Tagging a Harvested Big Game Animal

• Immediately after killing any big game animal, the appropriate tag must be validated.
• Cut out and completely remove the month and day of kill from the tag. A slit is not acceptable.
• Securely attach the tag to the carcass in a visible manner.
• One common method is using electrical tape on the antler.
• Washington tags have small holes on the right-hand side, which can be used to feed a zip tie through and attach it to an antler or ear.
tagging big game, hunting regulations, animal tagging

Skinning (1) -

Skinning an Elk
Standard Source: wdfw01807
Skinning the animal will help cool the meat faster. You can decide to skin the animal on the ground or hang it and skin it while it is hanging. Here are the steps for skinning an elk:

1. **Make small vertical cuts in the hind legs just below...
Skinning the animal will help cool the meat faster. You can decide to skin the animal on the ground or hang it and skin it while it is hanging. Here are the steps for skinning an elk:

1. Make small vertical cuts in the hind legs just below the ankle area, inside the ligament that controls the lower leg.
2. Put your gambrel hooks through those cuts.
3. Hoist the animal up.
4. Make a cut in the skin, but not into the meat around the hind leg, just below the point the elk is hanging. Go slow and make sure not to cut that tendon.
5. Make a cut from the previous step to the pelvis area where the meat is exposed.
6. Make little cuts along this line to create a flap you can hang on to.
7. Pull the skin away from the meat and cut the connective tissue, trying not to cut into the meat.
8. Once you have skinned the entire leg, repeat the previous four steps for the second hind leg.
9. If you are skinning at home, you can now cut the tail off.
10. Pull down on the skin to help separate it from the meat.
11. While holding downward pressure, cut the connective tissue, sometimes referred to as silver skin. Just run the knife along the edge where the meat and skin meet as you pull.
12. If you are going to want the skin tanned, try not to nick the hide.
13. Start working around the carcass and making the cuts as needed.
14. Once you get to the front legs, cut around the knee joint.
15. There is very little meat in the lower leg.
16. Once you have severed the tendons, if you bend the leg to the side it becomes easier to remove.
17. Do this on the other leg as well.
18. Now that the legs are off, continue skinning down the legs and onto the neck.
19. Skin down to about four inches from the skull.
20. Use your bone saw to cut through the spine just above where the skin is still attached to the carcass.
21. A hack saw could also be used, but make sure it is a clean blade.
22. At this point you can process the carcass yourself or check with a local butcher shop that may be able to process game animals for a fee.
skinning, elk, hunting, hide removal, preservation

Tag Reporting (1) -

Reporting Hunter Tags to WDFW

###...
Title: Reporting Hunter Tags to WDFW

Overview: Hunter reporting is an integral part of hunting any animal that requires a tag. It allows WDFW staff members to accurately measure the harvest and helps set future hunting seasons.

### Step-by-Step Process:
1. Go to [fishhunt.dfw.wa.gov](http://fishhunt.dfw.wa.gov).
2. Under the “I want to Submit” section on the left-hand side (Highlighted in Orange), select “Hunter Report”.
3. Select the “Submit Report” box in the top-left corner of the page.
4. Enter all customer information fields and click “GO”.
5. If an error occurs, such as “customer not found, please try your search again.”, verify the information that was entered.
6. Select the first species under the “Choose a tag to report on:” section.
7. Answer all questions that are on the screen. The questions will change based on the answers provided.
8. When completed, the report will issue a message that says, “You have finished the hunter report. Click FINISH to save all of your answers.” Click “FINISH” when completed.
9. A confirmation page will come up that shows the report has been submitted successfully.
10. Write down the submittal date and the confirmation number; this information may need to be referenced at a future date.
11. When completed, use the Back button on the screen and it will take you back to the page that shows which tags need to be reported on or have been reported.
12. Repeat the process for all tags with an outstanding report.

### Additional Information:
• This information is used to set future hunting seasons in conjunction with WDFW field staff population surveys.
• If you have trouble with the online system, you can also call 877-945-3492 and report by phone.
hunter reporting, tag submission, WDFW, hunting regulations, hunter education

Wildlife Health (1) -

Understanding and Reporting Elk Hoof Disease in Southwest Washington
High Priority Source: wdfw01807
Title: Understanding and Reporting Elk Hoof Disease in Southwest Washington

Overview: Over the past decade, the Washington Department of Fish and Wildlife (WDFW) has received a growing number of reports of elk hobbled by missing or...
Title: Understanding and Reporting Elk Hoof Disease in Southwest Washington

Overview: Over the past decade, the Washington Department of Fish and Wildlife (WDFW) has received a growing number of reports of elk hobbled by missing or misshapen hooves in southwest Washington. This is a major concern for hunters, area residents, and state wildlife managers.

### Key Information:
• Analysis of tissue from deformed hooves indicates the condition is likely caused by infectious treponeme bacteria, which have been linked to digital dermatitis in domestic sheep and cattle.
• A 16-member technical panel of veterinarians and researchers, formed by WDFW to review test results from affected elk, has supported these findings.

### Action Steps:
• For more information on Hoof Disease, please see the department’s website: [https://wdfw.wa.gov/species-habitats/diseases/elk-hoof](https://wdfw.wa.gov/species-habitats/diseases/elk-hoof)
• If you encounter an elk with hoof deformities, report it to WDFW for further investigation and monitoring.
elk hoof disease, infectious treponeme bacteria, WDFW, wildlife health reporting

Construct Traps and Snares for Hunting
High Priority Source: USMC Summer Survival Course Handbook
Objective: Construct traps and snares appropriate for the intended animal.

Objective: Construct traps and snares appropriate for the intended animal.

1. Choose a location that is likely to be frequented by the target animal (e.g., near water sources or food).
2. Use natural materials such as sticks, vines, and rope to construct the trap or snare.
3. Ensure that the loop size and ground clearance are appropriate for the intended animal.
4. Use bait to attract the animal into the trap or snare (e.g., meat, berries, or other food sources).
5. Check the trap regularly and adjust as needed to ensure it is functional.

General Considerations (1) -

List General Considerations to Take Game
Standard Source: USMC Winter Survival Course Handbook
Procedure:

1. Identify and understand the eight general considerations for taking game, which include:
- Knowledge of the terrain: Understand the environment where the game is likely to be found.
- Weather conditions: Be aware of...
Procedure:

1. Identify and understand the eight general considerations for taking game, which include:
- Knowledge of the terrain: Understand the environment where the game is likely to be found.
- Weather conditions: Be aware of how weather affects both the hunter and the game.
- Time of day: Know when different types of game are most active.
- Seasonal variations: Recognize changes in behavior and movement patterns based on seasons.
- Animal behavior: Understand the habits, feeding patterns, and escape routes of the target species.
- Legal regulations: Be familiar with local hunting laws and restrictions.
- Safety precautions: Ensure that all safety measures are followed to prevent accidents or injuries.
- Survival needs: Take only what is necessary for survival and avoid over-hunting.

Note: This list should be memorized and understood without the aid of references.
game taking considerations, hunting regulations, survival hunting, animal behavior

Throwing Weapons (1) -

Construct a Throwing Stick or Atlatl from Scavenged Materials
High Priority Source: Paleo Pocalypse
### Materials Required:

• Chair legs, table legs, discarded planks of wood, metal pipes meant for plumbing, or any similar rigid material.

### Steps:
1. Select the Material: Choose a straight and sturdy piece of scavenged material (wood or...
### Materials Required:

• Chair legs, table legs, discarded planks of wood, metal pipes meant for plumbing, or any similar rigid material.

### Steps:
1. Select the Material: Choose a straight and sturdy piece of scavenged material (wood or metal) that is approximately 2–3 feet in length.
2. Carve or Shape: If using wood, carve down the material to create a smooth, balanced stick. For metal pipes, ensure they are clean and free from sharp edges.
3. Create a Notch: Carve a small notch at one end of the stick (approximately 1–2 inches deep) for attaching the dart or projectile. This is essential for the atlatl function.
4. Attach Dart/Projectile: Secure a sharpened dart, arrow, or other projectile to the notch using natural fibers, paracord, or any available binding material.
5. Test and Adjust: Test the balance and effectiveness of your throwing stick or atlatl by practicing with it. Adjust as needed for better performance.

### Notes:
• Metal pipes can be used for heavier-duty throwing sticks but may require additional weight distribution to ensure proper balance.
• Ensure that all sharp edges are smoothed out to avoid injury during use.
throwing stick,atlatl,scavenged materials,hunting tools,post-apocalyptic weapons

Slings And Ammo (1) -

Create a Sling and Ammunition from Rubbish Materials
High Priority Source: Paleo Pocalypse
### Materials Required:

• Fabric-like, flexible material (e.g., clothing scraps, couch fabric, shower curtains)
• Cordage materials (paracord, twine, or other available string)
• Projectiles: Nuts, bolts, ball bearings, river rocks from landscaped...
### Materials Required:

• Fabric-like, flexible material (e.g., clothing scraps, couch fabric, shower curtains)
• Cordage materials (paracord, twine, or other available string)
• Projectiles: Nuts, bolts, ball bearings, river rocks from landscaped lawns.

### Steps:
1. Construct the Sling Pouch:
- Cut a piece of fabric-like material into a pouch shape (approximately 6–8 inches in length and 3–4 inches wide).
- If using paracord or twine, weave it into a durable pouch for added strength.
2. Attach the Sling Arms:
- Attach two long arms to each end of the pouch using cordage material. These arms should be approximately 18–24 inches in length.
3. Create Finger Loops:
- Tie a loop at the end of each arm for easy handling and release of the projectile.
4. Prepare Ammunition:
- Gather suitable projectiles such as nuts, bolts, ball bearings, or river rocks. Ensure they are clean and free from sharp edges.
5. Load and Use:
- Place a projectile into the pouch, pull it through one of the loops, and hold the other loop in your hand. Twist the sling to build momentum, then release to launch the projectile.

### Notes:
• For more durable slings, use paracord or twine for weaving the arms and pouch.
• Always test projectiles with a safe target before using them in hunting scenarios.
sling,ammunition,rubbish materials,hunting tools,post-apocalyptic weapons

Bamboo Weapons (1) -

Construct Bamboo Weapons for Hunting and Combat
High Priority Source: Paleo Pocalypse
### Materials Required:

• Bamboo stalks (available in landscaped lawns, parks, gardens)

### Steps:
1. Select the Bamboo: Choose a straight, sturdy bamboo stalk that is approximately 3–5 feet long and thick enough to withstand impact.
2....
### Materials Required:

• Bamboo stalks (available in landscaped lawns, parks, gardens)

### Steps:
1. Select the Bamboo: Choose a straight, sturdy bamboo stalk that is approximately 3–5 feet long and thick enough to withstand impact.
2. Prepare the Stalk:
- Cut the bamboo to the desired length using a sharp object (e.g., knife or broken glass).
- Smooth any rough edges with a stone or other available tool.
3. Create Spears or Gigs:
- Sharpen one end of the bamboo stalk by rubbing it against a hard surface until it becomes pointed and sharp enough for hunting.
4. Make Bows or Crossbows:
- Cut two shorter pieces from the bamboo (approximately 2–3 feet in length) to serve as limbs for the bow.
- Attach a string made from paracord, twine, or other available cordage between the ends of the limbs to form the bowstring.
5. Construct Arrows or Darts:
- Cut smaller pieces of bamboo (approximately 1–2 feet in length) and sharpen one end for use as arrows or darts.
6. Create Blowguns or Traps:
- Use hollow sections of bamboo to create blowguns by attaching a mouthpiece at one end and a small opening at the other.
- For primitive traps, cut slits into the bamboo stalks and shape them to form snares or pitfall mechanisms.

### Notes:
• Refer to the Yggdrasil Distro publication _Bamboo_ for detailed instructions on constructing each type of weapon.
• Ensure that all weapons are tested for safety before use in hunting scenarios.
bamboo,weapons,hunting tools,post-apocalyptic survival,bamboo uses

Trapper Responsibility (1) -

Understand the Commitment and Responsibility of Becoming a Trapper
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Trapping is a highly engaging, year-round activity that requires serious commitment, time, and dedication to responsible behavior. It is also a highly regulated activity due to public concerns about wildlife conservation and animal welfare....
Trapping is a highly engaging, year-round activity that requires serious commitment, time, and dedication to responsible behavior. It is also a highly regulated activity due to public concerns about wildlife conservation and animal welfare. Regulations are in place to ensure safe and selective trapping practices.

Trappers must be willing to spend significant time studying wildlife, scouting areas, preparing traps, working with landowners, setting traps, running traplines, and processing pelts. During trapping season, trappers are required to check their traps every day until they are removed.

Society, including both trappers and non-trappers, does not accept illegal or unethical behavior. This course will teach the basics of responsible trapping, but it is up to the individual to commit to ethical and legal practices.
trapping responsibility, wildlife conservation, animal welfare, trapper education

Furbearer Values (1) -

List Five Positive or Negative Values of Furbearers
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Furbearers have various ecological, biological, cultural, aesthetic, and economic values:

• Economic: Positive values include the use of furs, meat, and by-products such as perfume and fishing lures. Negative values include crop depredation,...
Furbearers have various ecological, biological, cultural, aesthetic, and economic values:

• Economic: Positive values include the use of furs, meat, and by-products such as perfume and fishing lures. Negative values include crop depredation, property damage, and flooded roads.

• Ecological: Furbearers have positive value as predators and prey in functioning ecosystems. However, excessive numbers can negatively impact habitats or prey on endangered animals.

• Cultural: Trapping is valued by many people as part of their cultural heritage. It involves outdoor skills, knowledge, respect for wildlife, and family activities. Some communities rely on trapping for food, clothing, and other resources.

• Biological: Furbearers provide positive values that help us understand human health and the effects of environmental pollutants. Negative biological values include exposure to diseases and parasites such as rabies and tularemia.

• Aesthetic: Furbearers have positive aesthetic value through their fur and wildlife watching opportunities.
furbearer values, ecological impact, cultural significance, economic importance, biological risks

Disease Prevention (1) -

Recognize Diseases Transmitted by Furbearers
High Priority Source: Student manual 2005
Furbearers can transmit diseases to humans, including:

• Rabies: A serious viral disease that affects the nervous system and is almost always fatal if left untreated.

• Tularemia: A bacterial infection that can cause fever, skin ulcers,...
Furbearers can transmit diseases to humans, including:

• Rabies: A serious viral disease that affects the nervous system and is almost always fatal if left untreated.

• Tularemia: A bacterial infection that can cause fever, skin ulcers, and swollen lymph nodes. It is typically transmitted through contact with infected animals or their bodily fluids.

Trappers should take precautions to avoid exposure to these diseases, such as wearing protective gloves and ensuring proper handling of trapped animals.
rabies, tularemia, disease prevention, trapping safety

Purpose: Understand which types of traps are legally allowed in your state for trapping activities.

Procedure:
1. Research and identify the legal trap types permitted by your state’s wildlife management agency.
2. States regulate trap legality based on factors such as animal welfare, efficiency, selectivity, and safety.
3. Common categories of traps include:
- Kill-type traps: Used to humanely kill animals (e.g., body-gripping traps).
- Live-restraining devices: Designed to capture animals without causing harm (e.g., foothold traps).
4. Some common trap types and their legality status are as follows:

6. Note that deadfalls and traps with teeth are often prohibited due to concerns about animal welfare.
7. Some states allow specific types of traps, such as submarine or colony traps for muskrats, depending on local regulations.
8. Be aware that trapping technology has evolved over nearly 200 years, and modern techniques may involve different trap designs and methods.
9. Raccoons and coyotes are widely distributed in the U.S., so ensure you understand which traps are appropriate for these species in your area.

1. Identify community members who may have different attitudes about furbearers and trapping.
2. Engage in respectful conversations to understand their perspectives on wildlife management and trapping.

Procedure:

1. Identify community members who may have different attitudes about furbearers and trapping.
2. Engage in respectful conversations to understand their perspectives on wildlife management and trapping.
3. Share information about the role of hunters and trappers in funding wildlife conservation efforts and habitat preservation.
4. Highlight success stories such as the recovery of species like elk, deer, geese, wild turkeys, wood ducks, beaver, bald eagles, and river otters due to conservation efforts.
5. Explain the North American Model of Wildlife Conservation, emphasizing that wildlife is a public resource managed for the benefit of all.
6. Address concerns about trapping by discussing regulations, ethical practices, and the importance of sustainable hunting and trapping.
7. Encourage participation in discussions about regulated trapping and its role in today’s society.
8. Promote understanding that responsible citizens have equal opportunities to participate in wildlife management through regulated hunting and trapping.
9. Use historical context, such as President Theodore Roosevelt's advocacy for public access to land for hunting, to support the importance of conservation.
10. Consider scenarios like encountering a farmer dealing with raccoon damage or meeting a new neighbor with differing views on meat consumption and wildlife management.

Trap Types (1) -

Identify Types of Live-Restraining Traps
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Identify live-restraining traps:

• Long-spring foothold traps: These are a common type of live-restraining trap with plain jaws.
• Double long-spring foothold traps: A variation of the long-spring trap, often used for trapping...
Identify live-restraining traps:

• Long-spring foothold traps: These are a common type of live-restraining trap with plain jaws.
• Double long-spring foothold traps: A variation of the long-spring trap, often used for trapping furbearers.
• Coil-spring foothold traps: Another type of live-restraining trap that uses a coil spring mechanism.
• Guarded traps: These are designed to prevent non-target animals from being caught.
• Enclosed foothold traps: These have additional enclosures or guards to protect non-target species.
• Cable devices: A type of live-restraining trap that uses cables to capture animals without causing harm.

Note: Foothold traps come in various sizes and strengths, each appropriate for specific species of furbearers. Underspring traps are no longer manufactured.
live-restraining traps, long-spring foothold trap, double long-spring trap, coil-spring trap, guarded trap, enclosed foothold trap, cable devices

Trap Jaw Characteristics (1) -

Identify and Understand Foothold Trap Jaw Characteristics and Modifications
Reference Source: Student manual 2005
Jaw Frame Characteristics and Modifications:

• Plain Jaws: Standard foothold trap jaws without any modifications.
• Padded Jaws: Padded foothold traps have rubber pads on the jaws to reduce injuries.
• Offset Jaws: Some designs use...
Jaw Frame Characteristics and Modifications:

• Plain Jaws: Standard foothold trap jaws without any modifications.
• Padded Jaws: Padded foothold traps have rubber pads on the jaws to reduce injuries.
• Offset Jaws: Some designs use offset jaws, which create a space between the gripping surfaces when the jaws are closed. The offset ranges from 1/8 to 1/4 inch.
• Double Jaws: These traps use two metal frames instead of one. One set of jaws is smaller and located inside the regular jaws.
• Laminated or Wide Jaws: Lamination increases jaw thickness and surface area for holding an animal’s foot. It is typically added by welding an additional strip of metal to the top or bottom of the jaw, flush with the original. Some trappers use double lamination, adding one strip above and one below the jaw.

Examples of Traps Mentioned:
• Silvertip Productions Guarded Foothold Trap
• Joe Goodman Coil-spring Padded Foothold Trap
• EGG™ Trap
• Spring-activated Cable Device
• Joe Goodman Laminated trap jaws
foot, foothold traps, jaw characteristics, padded jaws, offset jaws, double jaws, laminated jaws

Trapping Devices (1) -

Identify Relaxing and Non-Relaxing Locks
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Relaxing locks move in both directions on a cable. Non-relaxing locks only slide in one direction. If an animal pulls against the cable, it gets tighter, and will not release.
relaxing locks, non-relaxing locks, cable movement, trapping mechanics

Trapping Equipment (1) -

Proper Use of Swivels in Trapping Systems
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Purpose: To ensure safe and effective trapping by using swivels correctly.

Why Swivels Are Important:
• Reduce the chance of injury to animals by allowing traps to move freely in the same direction as the animal's foot.
• Prevent escape or...
Purpose: To ensure safe and effective trapping by using swivels correctly.

Why Swivels Are Important:
• Reduce the chance of injury to animals by allowing traps to move freely in the same direction as the animal's foot.
• Prevent escape or injury by ensuring the trap system functions properly.

Types of Swivels and Their Uses:
• Lap-link swivels, stake swivels, and universal swivels can be used to fasten a chain to a stake.
• When two stakes are needed, trappers use a special cross-staking swivel.
• Universal swivels (also called four-way swivels):
- Used in the middle of chains.
- Used to attach the chain to a trap at the center of the base-plate.
- Can be used in combination with sliding locks in submersion sets.

Installation and Use:
1. Choose high-quality swivels for your trap systems.
2. Secure chains to stakes using appropriate swivels (e.g., lap-link, stake, or universal).
3. For cross-staking setups, use a cross-staking swivel when two stakes are required.
4. Use universal swivels in the middle of chains and at the center of the base-plate for attaching to traps.
5. S-hooks can be used on some swivels. A special s-hook tool should be used to close the hook without damaging it.
6. Some trappers (e.g., coyote trappers) weld connections to prevent them from pulling open.

Warning: Always use the highest quality swivels in your trap systems to ensure safety and effectiveness.
swivels, trapping equipment, animal welfare, trap setup, universal swivel, lap-link swivel, stake swivel, cross-staking swivel

Trap Setup And Maintenance (1) -

Measuring Jaw Spread at the Dog and Hinge Posts
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Purpose: To ensure traps meet BMPs (Best Management Practices) or state regulations by accurately measuring jaw spread.

Why This Is Important:
• Traps must comply with specific jaw spread measurements to be legal and humane.
• Manufacturer...
Purpose: To ensure traps meet BMPs (Best Management Practices) or state regulations by accurately measuring jaw spread.

Why This Is Important:
• Traps must comply with specific jaw spread measurements to be legal and humane.
• Manufacturer designations such as “No. 2” coil-spring do not always indicate standardized measurements.

Measurement Steps:
1. Set the trap in a stable position for accurate measurement.
2. Measure the inside spread of the jaw frame at its widest point along the line from the dog to the opposite side (this is the jaw spread at the dog).
3. Measure the width between the two jaws where they connect to the hinge posts (this is the jaw spread at the hinge posts).
4. Be aware that slight differences in jaw spread measurements may occur on the same make and model of traps.

Tips:
• Use a reliable measuring tool for accuracy.
• Double-check measurements if you are unsure about compliance with local regulations.
• Always ensure the trap is functioning properly after measurement.
jaw spread, trap measurement, BMPs, state regulations, trapping compliance, trap setup

Trap Practice (1) -

Practice Setting and Releasing a Kill-Type Trap Safely
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
To practice setting and releasing a kill-type trap safely, follow these steps:

1. Select the trap: Choose a common kill-type trap for practice.
2. Prepare the trap: Ensure that the trap is clean and free of any debris or obstructions.
3....
To practice setting and releasing a kill-type trap safely, follow these steps:

1. Select the trap: Choose a common kill-type trap for practice.
2. Prepare the trap: Ensure that the trap is clean and free of any debris or obstructions.
3. Set the trap: Follow the manufacturer's instructions to set the trap properly.
4. Check placement: Ensure that the trap is securely positioned and that all components are fastened correctly.
5. Release the trap safely: Practice releasing the trap with an instructor or experienced trapper until you can do it correctly.
6. Reset the trap: After practice, reset the trap for future use.

Important safety considerations:
• Always have an instructor or experienced trapper present when practicing setting and releasing a kill-type trap.
• Use gloves to protect your hands from injury and to avoid leaving human scent on the trap.
• Practice with the same type of gloves you will use when making sets on the trapline.
• Never attempt to set or release a kill-type trap without proper training and tools.
kill-type trap, practice setting, safety procedures, trapper education

Clothing Equipment (1) -

Select Appropriate Clothing for Trapping in Various Weather Conditions
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Procedure:

1. Choose Sturdy Footwear:
- Wear sturdy rubber boots with non-slip soles for rough terrain, snow, or ice.
- Ensure the boots are free of unusual scents to avoid attracting animals.

2. **Layer Clothing for Temperature...
Procedure:

1. Choose Sturdy Footwear:
- Wear sturdy rubber boots with non-slip soles for rough terrain, snow, or ice.
- Ensure the boots are free of unusual scents to avoid attracting animals.

2. Layer Clothing for Temperature Regulation:
- Dress in layers that can be removed as temperatures rise during the day.
- In cold weather, wear wool clothing because it retains heat even when wet and allows perspiration to evaporate.
- Use thermal underwear on the coldest days for added warmth.

3. Use Rain Gear:
- Carry a lightweight parka or rain suit to stay dry and block wind.

4. Maintain Cleanliness of Clothing:
- Keep all clothing clean and free of unusual scents, as predatory animals like foxes and coyotes are wary of certain scents.

5. Choose Quiet Clothing for Visibility Control:
- Avoid clothing that makes noise when walking to increase the chances of spotting wildlife.
- Use hunter orange clothing during hunting seasons for visibility and personal safety, even if it may make you more visible to potential trap thieves.

6. Select Appropriate Water Gear:
- For water trapping, use hip boots or waders.
- Shallow water trappers can use hip boots, while deep water trappers should wear chest waders for warmth and buoyancy.
- Consider wearing an inflatable personal flotation device (PFD) for safety in deep water. These vests expand when needed by pulling a string to release gas into the vest.
- Carry a mouth tube as a backup in case the gas canister fails.

7. Protect Hands and Arms:
- Water trappers should wear long rubber gloves to protect against cold water.
- Canine trappers may use two pairs of gloves, one for handling traps to keep them scent-free.

8. Wear Warm Hats:
- Wear a warm hat to prevent body heat loss through the head and to protect the face from sun and wind.

9. Carry Navigation Tools:
- Always carry a map and compass, and store them in the same place for quick access during emergencies.

10. Use Lighting Equipment:
- Carry a flashlight to follow trails, be visible to hunters, or signal for help if lost, injured, or ill.
trapping,clothing,equipment,weather conditions,winter trapping,rain gear,water trappers,footwear,gloves,hats,navigation tools,lighting equipment

Trapline Equipment (1) -

Identify and Prepare Trapping Equipment for a Trapline
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
### Identify Tools, Materials, and Supplies Needed to Make Sets and Run a Trapline

Beginning trappers should start with basic gear needed to trap one or two species of furbearers. If you need to buy all new equipment, you will spend a lot of money....
### Identify Tools, Materials, and Supplies Needed to Make Sets and Run a Trapline

Beginning trappers should start with basic gear needed to trap one or two species of furbearers. If you need to buy all new equipment, you will spend a lot of money. Learn to be successful with basic gear so you can make some spending money from fur sales before you invest too much. As you gain experience, you will also learn where to get good prices on equipment and develop a better sense of the gear needed for other types of trapping.

You can purchase used equipment to save money. Be careful about buying used waders or hip boots. Old boots and waders may leak. Check used traps to make certain they are legal and in good condition before you buy them. Trap springs may weaken over time.

Trap Tags - Check your state trapping regulations for requirements to tag your traps. Many states require the trapper to have his or her name and address attached to each trap.

### Essential Tools and Materials
• Gloves:
- Gauntlet gloves are used by water trappers to keep dry in cold weather.
- Latex gloves are used when skinning animals.
- Rubber or cotton trap setting gloves help land trappers avoid leaving human scent on traps.
• PFD (Personal Flotation Device): An inexpensive item that can save your life. Always wear one when working near water.
• Ice Picks: Keep them where you can reach them fast. If you fall through ice, they are essential for pulling yourself out of deep water.
• Trap Stakes & Grapples: Steel stakes are needed to anchor traps. Know the length and size required based on specific furbearers and soil conditions. You may need grapples in certain sets.
• Pliers and Cable Cutters: Used for trap adjustments, cutting, and bending wire. If aircraft cable is used for snares or anchoring systems, you will also need cable cutters.
• Hatchet: Used for cutting limbs, driving stakes, chopping ice, and making certain kinds of sets.
• Wire or Aircraft Cable (3/32 or 1/8 inch): Can be used to make submersion sets and fasten traps. Wire can also support cable devices.
• Trapping Staff: Used for checking water depths when wading, detecting underwater dens, retrieving traps from the water, and dispatching animals caught in live-restraining traps.
• Trowel: Used to make dirt holes or pocket sets in water.
• Bucket, Bag, and Pack Basket: Any of these can be used to carry equipment and traps.
• Knives: Folding lock back knives are recommended for trappers. They have many uses on the trapline.
• Dirt Sifter: A frame about eight inches square and three inches deep with a quarter inch mesh screen on the bottom. Used to cover traps with fine soil, removing rocks or chunks of dirt that could interfere with the trap closing properly.
• Pan Covers: Recommended to keep dirt and debris from getting under the trap pan on land sets. Options include wax paper, screen, plastic, and clean patches of cloth.
• Trapper’s Cap: Can be used instead of pan covers. This device temporarily fits over the trap pan while dirt is packed inside the jaws. When removed, it leaves the area beneath the pan free of dirt.
• Underalls: Some trappers use pieces of foam rubber or fiberglass insulation cut to the shape of the trap pan and thickness of the space under the pan. This helps keep dirt and debris from getting under the pan.
• Catchpole (Release Noose): Used to hold an animal so it can be safely released or dispatched. An essential tool for a land trapper.
• Kneeling Pad: Land trappers use cloth, canvas, or rubber pads to kneel on when making land sets. Helps keep human odor off the set and is also a good place to put dirt when digging the bed for a trap.
trapping, equipment, tools, materials, supplies, trapline, gloves, pfd, ice picks, trap stakes, grapples, pliers, cable cutters, hatchet, wire, aircraft cable, trapping staff, trowel, bucket, bag, pack basket, knives, dirt sifter, pan covers, trapper's cap, underalls, catchpole

Attracting Furbearers (1) -

Using Bait, Lure, and Urine to Attract Furbearers
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Procedure for Using Bait, Lure, and Urine to Attract Specific Furbearers

1. Understand the Target Animal's Habits: Research the food sources, eating habits, and scent preferences of the furbearer you are trying to attract.
2. **Select...
Procedure for Using Bait, Lure, and Urine to Attract Specific Furbearers

1. Understand the Target Animal's Habits: Research the food sources, eating habits, and scent preferences of the furbearer you are trying to attract.
2. Select Appropriate Bait: Choose baits based on the target animal’s diet:
- Meat and Fish Baits: Use fresh, tainted, or liquid forms of meat or fish for animals with a strong sense of smell.
- Plant-Based Baits: Use corn, carrots, or apples for animals that consume plant matter.
3. Avoid Non-Target Animals: Be cautious when using baits such as uncovered flesh (which may attract hawks and owls) or corn (which can attract a wide range of non-target wildlife).
4. Use Covered Flesh Baits: Lightly cover meat or fish bait to make it more attractive to furbearers, which rely heavily on their sense of smell.
5. Consider Visual Attractants: In areas where legal, use visual lures such as strips of cloth or pieces of metal that flutter in the breeze (e.g., for bobcats).
6. Use Lures Strategically:
- Glandular Lures: Use scents that appeal to an animal’s sexual attraction or territorial instincts.
- Food Lures: Use scents that mimic food sources to attract animals based on their hunger.
- Curiosity Lures: Use unfamiliar objects or scents to trigger an animal's instinct to investigate.
7. Combine Bait and Lure Techniques: Use combinations of bait, lure, and urine for maximum effectiveness in attracting specific furbearers.
8. Follow Regulations: Always adhere to local trapping regulations regarding the use of baits and lures.
bait,lure,urine,furbearers,trapping,hunting,animal attraction

Trap Baiting Techniques (1) -

Use Baits and Lures to Attract Target Species and Deter Non-Target Animals
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Purpose: Select appropriate baits and lures to attract target species while avoiding non-target animals.

Procedure:
1. Select Appropriate Bait: Use natural food sources that are attractive to the specific furbearing animal you are...
Purpose: Select appropriate baits and lures to attract target species while avoiding non-target animals.

Procedure:
1. Select Appropriate Bait: Use natural food sources that are attractive to the specific furbearing animal you are targeting. Avoid using pet food or other baits that may attract dogs, cats, or other non-target animals.
2. Use Glandular Lures: Employ glandular lures that appeal to a specific animal's mating instincts for increased effectiveness.
3. Avoid Attractive Baits Near Domestic Areas: If trapping near homes with pets, avoid using fish or other baits that may attract cats or dogs.

Notes:
• Always ensure that the bait is placed in a way that minimizes access to non-target animals.
• Use only natural lures and baits that are known to be effective for the target species.
baits, lures, selective trapping, non-target deterrence, glandular lures, pet food avoidance

Trap Tuning Techniques (1) -

Properly Tune BMP Traps for Selectivity and Efficiency
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Purpose: Ensure that BMP traps are properly tuned to maximize selectivity and efficiency in trapping.

Procedure:
1. Select the Right Trap Size: Choose a trap with an appropriate jaw spread and spring strength based on the target...
Purpose: Ensure that BMP traps are properly tuned to maximize selectivity and efficiency in trapping.

Procedure:
1. Select the Right Trap Size: Choose a trap with an appropriate jaw spread and spring strength based on the target species.
2. Adjust Pan Tension: Set pan tension according to the species being trapped:
- 1 pound for gray foxes
- 2 pounds for red foxes or bobcats
- 4 pounds for coyotes
3. Refer to BMP Guidelines: Consult the “Traps” chapter in your manual for detailed instructions on tuning traps and adjusting pan tension.

Notes:
• Properly tuned traps are more effective at capturing target species without harming non-target animals.
• Always test traps before use to ensure they function correctly.
BMP traps, trap tuning, pan tension, selectivity, efficiency, jaw spread, spring strength

Trap Placement Guidelines (1) -

Avoid Trails and Areas Used by Livestock, Domestic Animals, Non-Target Wildlife, and Humans
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Purpose: Minimize the risk of trapping non-target animals or interfering with human activity.

Procedure:
1. Choose Remote Locations: Avoid setting traps on trails that are frequently used by people, pets, livestock, or other...
Purpose: Minimize the risk of trapping non-target animals or interfering with human activity.

Procedure:
1. Choose Remote Locations: Avoid setting traps on trails that are frequently used by people, pets, livestock, or other wildlife.
2. Avoid Hunting Areas: Do not trap in areas where hunters and dogs may be active, especially during seasons when pheasants, quail, grouse, raccoons, or other dog-hunted species are being targeted.
3. Coordinate with Property Users: Make friends with people who use the property you are trapping on to avoid conflicts and ensure safe trap placement.
4. Avoid Areas with Regular Pet Exercise: Do not place traps in areas where pets are regularly exercised, as this increases the risk of non-target animals being caught.

Notes:
• Trap placement is a critical factor in ensuring selectivity and minimizing unintended captures.
• Always be aware of local regulations and property usage patterns before setting traps.
trap placement, remote areas, livestock avoidance, non-target deterrence, human activity, property coordination

Importance of planning when, where, and how to trap on public land:

1. Focus on water trapping during times of heavy public use for hunting to avoid catching dogs.
2. Most furbearers are nocturnal, so set traps in the evening and check them the next morning.
3. Consult local managers, rangers, or wildlife officers to identify heavily used hunting areas.
4. Avoid these areas when hunters are running dogs.

How variations in trap placement can increase selectivity:

2. Reduces chance of catching a non-target animal due to selective placement.
3. Less chance an animal will escape, increasing trapping efficiency.

Water Sets (1) -

Create a Sliding Wire Submersion Set for Aquatic Furbearers
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Procedure:

To create a sliding wire submersion set for aquatic furbearers such as muskrat, mink, beaver, nutria, and river otter, follow these steps:

1. Attach a sliding lock to the end of your trap chain. The lock will prevent the animal...
Procedure:

To create a sliding wire submersion set for aquatic furbearers such as muskrat, mink, beaver, nutria, and river otter, follow these steps:

1. Attach a sliding lock to the end of your trap chain. The lock will prevent the animal from swimming back toward shallow water.
2. Use a heavy object (such as a rock) or a stake for an anchor. If using a stake, push it into the stream bed in deep water.
3. Attach a wire to the anchor or stake. Ensure the wire is strong enough to hold the trap and animal underwater.
4. Submerge the anchor or stake in water deep enough to fully submerge the target furbearer. This ensures that the animal will be pulled under once trapped.
5. Bring the wire to the shoreline. Position the sliding lock so it points toward deeper water, allowing the trap to slide down the wire toward the deeper area but not back toward shallow water.
6. Attach the free end of the wire to a stake on the bank near your set. Drive this stake into the ground securely to anchor the system.
7. Ensure the sliding wire is tight. This will prevent any slack that could allow the animal to escape or become tangled.
8. Make your set by attaching the trap to the chain and positioning it in the water. The trap should be placed where the target furbearer is likely to swim toward deep water, such as near a muskrat den, channel, or pocket in the bank.

Important Notes:
• This technique takes advantage of the animal's instinct to swim toward deeper water when trapped.
• Ensure that the trap is set at an appropriate depth and location for the target species.
• Always check local regulations regarding trapping near muskrat lodges or other sensitive areas.
sliding wire, submersion set, aquatic furbearers, muskrat trapping, water sets, hunting techniques

Animal Handling (1) -

Thawing an Animal Frozen in a Body-Gripping Trap
Reference Source: Student manual 2005
Procedure:

1. Identify the location of the frozen animal trapped in the body-gripping trap.
2. Carefully approach the trap to avoid causing further harm to the animal or yourself.
3. Use warm water or a heat source to begin thawing the animal...
Procedure:

1. Identify the location of the frozen animal trapped in the body-gripping trap.
2. Carefully approach the trap to avoid causing further harm to the animal or yourself.
3. Use warm water or a heat source to begin thawing the animal slowly and gently.
4. Ensure that the area is safe for both you and the animal during the thawing process.
5. Once the animal is fully thawed, carefully remove it from the trap using appropriate tools.
6. Monitor the animal closely after removal to ensure it recovers properly.

Details:
• Thawing an animal frozen in a body-gripping trap helps prevent fur damage and ensures the animal's well-being.
• Use caution when handling any trapped animal, even if it is frozen.
• Always follow local regulations regarding the use of body-gripping traps and ensure compliance with wildlife conservation laws.
thawing animal,body gripping trap,animal handling

Land Trap Sets (1) -

Selecting Safe and Effective Land Set Locations
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Objective: Identify good places to make land sets that ensure animal welfare, selectivity, and trapper safety.

### Good Places for Land Sets
• Brush rows and fencerows: These guide animal movements and provide food sources such as rodents...
Objective: Identify good places to make land sets that ensure animal welfare, selectivity, and trapper safety.

### Good Places for Land Sets
• Brush rows and fencerows: These guide animal movements and provide food sources such as rodents or birds for furbearers.
• Areas near farm lanes: Choose locations where farm lanes intersect changing cover types or pass through brush rows. These areas are frequented by furbearers like raccoons and opossums.
• Old dumps: Furbearers often hunt for food in old dump sites, making these effective locations for land sets.

### Considerations When Choosing Locations
• Avoid setting traps near homes or places heavily used by people and their pets.
• Ensure the location minimizes exposure to domestic animals and human activities.
• Choose areas that prevent entanglement with fences or other objects that might cause injury.
• Avoid trails used by people.

### Additional Recommendations
• Use steel stakes on land for secure and durable trap sets.
land set locations, brush rows, fencerows, farm lanes, old dumps, steel stakes, animal welfare, selectivity, trapper safety

Trap Setting (1) -

Cover a Foothold Trap with Dirt, Leaves, or Grass
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Proper Method for Covering a Foothold Trap Set on Land

• Use dirt, leaves, and grass to cover your trap. The covering must not interfere with the action of the trap.

• Ensure that nothing gets under the trap pan, or the trap...
Proper Method for Covering a Foothold Trap Set on Land

• Use dirt, leaves, and grass to cover your trap. The covering must not interfere with the action of the trap.

• Ensure that nothing gets under the trap pan, or the trap may not work properly.

• Make sure there are no objects above the jaws that might prevent the trap from closing correctly.

• Crumple up a piece of wax paper, unfold it, and use it as a trap cover. This softens the wax paper so it won’t make noise when an animal steps on it.

• Use a dirt sifter to cover your trap without getting small sticks or stones in your set.

• For raccoons or opossums, you can use just a few leaves or grass for covering the trap.
covering traps,dirt,grass,wax paper,trap setting

Trap Modification (1) -

Use Enclosures to Prevent Non-Target Animal Capture in Body-Gripping Traps
High Priority Source: Student manual 2005
To reduce the risk of capturing non-target animals when using body-gripping traps, follow these steps:

1. Enclose body-gripping traps within a box or enclosure that limits access to only target species.
2. **Determine the appropriate size of...
To reduce the risk of capturing non-target animals when using body-gripping traps, follow these steps:

1. Enclose body-gripping traps within a box or enclosure that limits access to only target species.
2. Determine the appropriate size of the opening based on the target animal’s dimensions to ensure selectivity.
3. Place the trap in a location where non-target animals are unlikely to encounter it, such as near burrows or trails used by target species.
4. Check local regulations to confirm whether enclosing traps is legal in your area and follow any specific guidelines provided.
5. Monitor traps regularly to ensure that enclosures remain intact and functioning properly.
6. Remove the trap from use if it is not selective enough, or modify the enclosure as needed to improve selectivity.

Important Considerations:
• Enclosures should be constructed with durable materials to prevent damage or tampering by animals.
• Ensure that the enclosure does not cause harm or distress to any animal, including non-target species.
• Always use enclosures in conjunction with other trapping methods if necessary.
body-gripping traps, enclosure use, trap selectivity, non-target prevention, animal welfare

Cable Devices Handling (1) -

Proper Handling and Storage of Cable Devices
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Proper Handling and Storage of Cable Devices

1. Use a strong wire to remove the cable devices from the hot water.
2. Allow them to dry completely.
3. Once cooled, handle them with gloves that are free of any scent.
4. Hang the...
Proper Handling and Storage of Cable Devices

1. Use a strong wire to remove the cable devices from the hot water.
2. Allow them to dry completely.
3. Once cooled, handle them with gloves that are free of any scent.
4. Hang the devices in a dry place where they will not absorb any unnatural odors.

Additional Notes:
• Prepare enough cable devices to last you the season.
• Discard cables after capturing an animal, as they may kink and weaken after use.
• Inspect all other parts of the cable device for damage or weakening before using them again.
cable devices, handling, storage, gloves, scent-free, drying

Cable Devices Usage (1) -

Setting Selective Cable Device Traps
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Setting Selective Cable Device Traps

1. Set cable devices in locations where the animal cannot contact brush, fences, or other objects.
2. Prevent the animal from reaching anything it could climb over by **suspending it in the device with...
Setting Selective Cable Device Traps

1. Set cable devices in locations where the animal cannot contact brush, fences, or other objects.
2. Prevent the animal from reaching anything it could climb over by suspending it in the device with its feet off the ground.
3. Use shorter cables to reduce the chance of the animal causing entanglement or injury.
4. Ensure that animals caught in cable devices have freedom of movement and are not likely to hurt themselves unless they tangle the cable on something.

Additional Notes:
• Entanglement is a concern when using cable devices.
• Animals caught in cable devices should be monitored for signs of distress or injury.
selective trapping, cable device sets, entanglement prevention, animal safety

Aquatic Furbearer Trapping (1) -

Using Cable Devices for Aquatic Furbearers
High Priority Source: Student manual 2005
Using Cable Devices for Aquatic Furbearers

1. Cable devices can be set on land or in water, commonly used for trapping beaver.
2. To increase selectivity, set cable devices underwater.
3. Attach cables to stout poles and stick...
Using Cable Devices for Aquatic Furbearers

1. Cable devices can be set on land or in water, commonly used for trapping beaver.
2. To increase selectivity, set cable devices underwater.
3. Attach cables to stout poles and stick them in the mud to create channel sets or baited sets for beaver.
4. During winter, trappers can chop a hole in the ice, push poles through the hole into the mud with cable devices baited for beaver.
5. The under-ice beaver set is one of the rare times when bait is used with a cable device.
6. Cable devices can also be set as live-restraining traps in water, anchored on land to allow furbearers to leave the water.

Additional Notes:
• Regulations for cable devices vary by state and depend on furbearer management needs.
• Trappers should ensure compliance with local laws regarding selective trapping.
beaver trapping, aquatic furbearers, cable devices in water, under-ice sets

Dress neatly when approaching landowners.

Be polite, even if denied permission.

When speaking with landowners, ask about potential issues such as:
• Too many furbearers
• Neighbors who may want trapping done on their property

Establish a reputation as a responsible trapper. This can lead to landowners contacting you directly for trapping opportunities.

Contact landowners again shortly before the season opens, and ask about:
• Other users of the property (e.g., hunters)
• Provide details such as:
- Days and times you will be on their property
- Type of vehicle you plan to drive
• Ensure they have your telephone number in case they need to reach you.

Obtaining permission early allows for:
• Ample time for pre-season scouting
• Respectful treatment of the land and its owner during trapping activities

Plan the materials you need before scouting.

• Set traps quickly when the season opens
• Avoid wasting time during the season

Avoid waiting until the season opens to scout, as it can be:
• Time-consuming

• May alert wary furbearers (e.g., fox and coyotes)

• Set traps quickly without disturbing the area
• Minimize disturbance to wildlife

Journaling And Recordkeeping (1) -

Maintain a Daily Trapping Journal
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Why keep a trapping journal?

Keeping a daily trapping journal is essential for several reasons:

• Increase your success: By recording details about trap types, set locations, and catch rates, you can refine your techniques over time.

-...
Why keep a trapping journal?

Keeping a daily trapping journal is essential for several reasons:

• Increase your success: By recording details about trap types, set locations, and catch rates, you can refine your techniques over time.

• Guide others to your traps if you get sick: In the event of illness or injury, notes in your journal can help others locate your traps and continue managing them.

• Save your memories: Your journal will preserve personal experiences and achievements from each trapping season.

What to include in your journal?

• Types of traps used
• How you set your traps
• Number of animals caught at each trap location before removal
• Different lures or baits tested
• Sketches of trap sets for reference
• Notes on seasonal variations and how they affect trapping success
trapping,journal,recordkeeping,hunting,trapsets,notes

Furbearer Utilization And Sales (1) -

Properly Handle and Utilize Harvested Furbearers
Reference Source: Student manual 2005
Full Use of Harvested Furbearers

Responsible trappers should make full use of furbearers they harvest. This includes:

• Pelts for clothing: High-quality pelts are valuable for making garments.
• Human food and pet food: Meat from...
Full Use of Harvested Furbearers

Responsible trappers should make full use of furbearers they harvest. This includes:

• Pelts for clothing: High-quality pelts are valuable for making garments.
• Human food and pet food: Meat from furbearers can be used as a source of nutrition.
• Glands, skulls, and fertilizer: These byproducts have additional uses in various industries.

Selling Options for Furbearers or Pelts

There are four main ways to sell furbearers or pelts:

1. Local furbuyers: They provide local knowledge and can offer guidance on fur handling techniques. Local buyers often purchase whole animals, green pelts (skinned but not fl eshed, stretched, or dried), and may be a good option if you lack storage or processing facilities.

2. Traveling furbuyers: These buyers may visit multiple locations and can offer competitive prices for large quantities of fur.

3. Selling by mail: This method allows trappers to reach a wider market but requires proper packaging and shipping methods.

4. Fur auctions: Auctions provide an opportunity to sell furs to the highest bidder, potentially offering better prices for rare or high-quality pelts.

Considerations When Selling

• Animals with unusual pelts (e.g., albinos) may fetch higher prices from taxidermists than local buyers.
• Lesser-trapped species like ringtails may have different market values depending on the buyer.
• Always check current regulations before selling furs to ensure compliance with legal requirements.
furbearers,utilization,selling,pelts,trapping,hunting

Legal Obligations (1) -

Understand Legal and Social Obligations of Trapping
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Legal and social obligations for trappers include:

1. Follow trapping regulations: This includes seasons, trap types, sets, permission to trap, and public safety.
2. Consequences of non-compliance: Failing to follow regulations can...
Legal and social obligations for trappers include:

1. Follow trapping regulations: This includes seasons, trap types, sets, permission to trap, and public safety.
2. Consequences of non-compliance: Failing to follow regulations can result in fines, jail time, loss of licenses, disapproval from other trappers, and outdoor users.
3. Social acceptance as a trapper: To be accepted by the trapping community, you must know and follow all regulations.

Why it matters:
• Trapping is considered a privilege, not a right.
• Society expects trappers to behave responsibly.
• Regulations help conserve wildlife resources and ensure public safety.
• Ethical decisions are based on knowledge, skills, attitudes, and experience.
trapping regulations, legal obligations, ethical trapping, social responsibility

Ethics (1) -

Understand the Role of Ethics in Trapping
High Priority Source: Student manual 2005
Ethics is a system of principles for good conduct, and it plays an important role in the behavior of trappers, hunters, and anglers.

• Ethics deals with right or wrong: What is considered ethical in one situation may not be in another. For...
Ethics is a system of principles for good conduct, and it plays an important role in the behavior of trappers, hunters, and anglers.

• Ethics deals with right or wrong: What is considered ethical in one situation may not be in another. For example:
- If beaver are causing damage on a property, you may choose to take as many as possible.
- If beaver are scarce on another property, you should only take a few.
• Ethical behavior requires judgment: You must use your knowledge, skills, attitudes, and experience to decide what is right or wrong.
• Learn from mentors: You can learn ethical behavior from family members or trusted mentors.

Why it matters:
• Ethical decisions help maintain the trust of other trappers, outdoor users, and the public.
• Ethics supports conservation efforts and ensures responsible use of wildlife resources.
trapping ethics, ethical behavior, animal welfare, conservation

Scats refer to animal droppings or feces.

• These can be used to identify:
- The species of an animal.
- Its diet and health.
- Its movement patterns.
• When handling scats:
1. Wear gloves to avoid contamination.
2. Store samples in a sealed container for analysis.
3. Avoid direct contact with scats, especially from unknown or potentially dangerous animals.
• Scats can also be used as evidence in wildlife investigations.
