Trap Recovery (1) -

Use a Trap Hook for Recovery and Wading
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Definition: A pole with a hook at one end to help find and recover traps from water. Often used as a wading stick.

Action Steps:
1. Select a trap hook that is appropriate for the size of the water body and type of trap being recovered.
2....
Definition: A pole with a hook at one end to help find and recover traps from water. Often used as a wading stick.

Action Steps:
1. Select a trap hook that is appropriate for the size of the water body and type of trap being recovered.
2. Use the hook to locate submerged or hidden traps in water.
3. Retrieve the trap using the hook, ensuring it is done safely and without damaging the trap.
4. When wading through shallow water, use the trap hook as a support tool for balance and stability.
5. Inspect the trap for damage after recovery and before reuse.
trap hook, trap recovery, wading stick, hunting trapping

Archery Equipment Regulations (1) -

Use Archery Equipment For Turkey Hunting In Washington State
Standard Source: wdfw01803
Procedure:

1. Ensure your archery equipment meets the legal requirements for turkey hunting in Washington State:
- Mechanical broadheads are legal for all archery hunting, including with crossbows.
- It is unlawful to attach any...
Procedure:

1. Ensure your archery equipment meets the legal requirements for turkey hunting in Washington State:
- Mechanical broadheads are legal for all archery hunting, including with crossbows.
- It is unlawful to attach any electrical equipment or electric devices, except illuminated nocks, to the bow or arrow while hunting.
- Do not shoot a bow and arrow from a vehicle or from, across, or along the maintained portion of a public highway.
- It is unlawful to use any device secured to or supported by the bow for maintaining it at full draw or in a firing position.
- Scopes are prohibited on bows used for hunting.

2. Choose between compound, traditional, and crossbow equipment:
- Compound bows have mechanical let-off, reducing draw weight significantly at full draw (up to 85%), making them easier to use.
- Traditional bows include longbows or recurve bows, which lack mechanical let-off and require more strength but are equally effective if the hunter is proficient.
- Crossbows can be used for turkey hunting. Mechanical broadheads are legal to use with crossbows. Guillotine broadheads can also be used with crossbows, but they should only be used if you are 100% confident in your ability to accurately hit the target.

3. Follow these restrictions:
- It is unlawful to discharge a crossbow from a vehicle or from, across, or along the maintained portion of a public highway.

4. Choose appropriate broadheads for hunting:
- Use mechanical broadheads for all archery hunting, including with crossbows.
- Guillotine broadheads are also legal but should be used only by experienced hunters due to their specialized design and potential risks.
archery equipment, turkey hunting, Washington State, crossbows, mechanical broadheads, guillotine broadheads

Field Equipment Construction (1) -

Constructing a Custom Ground Blind for Hunting
Standard Source: wdfw01803 + wdfw01807
Materials Needed: Burlap, 1 x 1’s (wooden boards), spray paint, string, drill

Steps:
1. Cut the Lumber: Cut the 1 x 1’s into sections approximately four feet in length.
2. Drill Holes: Drill evenly spaced holes along the length of...
Materials Needed: Burlap, 1 x 1’s (wooden boards), spray paint, string, drill

Steps:
1. Cut the Lumber: Cut the 1 x 1’s into sections approximately four feet in length.
2. Drill Holes: Drill evenly spaced holes along the length of each 1 x 1 piece to allow for lacing burlap through them.
3. Paint the Wood: Spray paint the wood with a dark color and add streaks of green, black, and tan to blend it into natural surroundings.
4. Lace the Burlap: Thread the burlap through the drilled holes in the 1 x 1’s and secure it using string or other fastening methods.
5. Assemble the Blind: Arrange the laced pieces together to form a blind structure, ensuring that all sides are covered with burlap for concealment.
6. Conceal the Blind: Place natural vegetation such as grass, cattails, or sagebrush around the blind to help it blend into the environment.
7. Position the Blind: Set up the blind in a location where it is fully concealed by placing brush or natural cover around it. Keep windows in the back zipped up to avoid silhouetting yourself. Use natural vegetation from the hunting site to "brush up" the blind for better concealment.
ground blind, hunting, burlap, camouflage, construction

Shooting Techniques For Big Game (1) -

Taking a Broadside and Quartering Away Shot on an Elk or Deer
Standard Source: wdfw01807
**Broadside Shot:

Step 1:** Identify the broadside shot opportunity, which is the most effective and easiest for inexperienced hunters.

Step 2: Aim at the vital organs, typically both lungs and possibly the heart.

Step 3: Ensure you are...
**Broadside Shot:

Step 1:** Identify the broadside shot opportunity, which is the most effective and easiest for inexperienced hunters.

Step 2: Aim at the vital organs, typically both lungs and possibly the heart.

Step 3: Ensure you are confident in your shot placement before taking the shot.

Step 4: Practice with your equipment to improve accuracy and confidence.


**Quartering Away Shot:

Step 1:** Identify the quartering away shot opportunity, which is effective but can be challenging for some hunters.

Step 2: Aim at the tail end of the lung that faces you and the middle or front of the lung that faces away from you.

Step 3: Target approximately four ribs in from the tail of the animal.

Step 4: Practice with your equipment to improve accuracy and confidence in taking this shot.
broadside shot, quartering away shot, elk hunting, deer hunting, shooting techniques, vital organs

Body-Gripping Traps (1) -

Use Body-Gripping Traps Safely and Effectively
Reference Source: Student manual 2005
Body-gripping traps, also known as Conibear™ traps, are commonly used in water sets for mink, muskrat, and beaver. They consist of two rotating jaws that close on an animal's neck or chest when triggered. Larger body-gripping traps should be...
Body-gripping traps, also known as Conibear™ traps, are commonly used in water sets for mink, muskrat, and beaver. They consist of two rotating jaws that close on an animal's neck or chest when triggered. Larger body-gripping traps should be used with caution, especially on land, to avoid capturing non-target species.

Proper Use:
1. Set the trap so it closes from top to bottom for optimal function.
2. Always use the buddy system when using large body-gripping traps to prevent accidental injury.
3. If a trap is accidentally sprung on your hand or arm, it can be difficult to release. In such cases, use a rope with a loop in one end, as described elsewhere in this manual, to free yourself. To do so: thread the rope through the ends of the springs, put your foot in the loop, and use your free arm to pull the loose end.
4. Always use a safety gripper when setting large body-gripping traps.
5. Carry setting tongs and a length of rope with a loop in the end. Keep it in a pocket where you can easily reach it with one hand.

Trigger Adjustments for Selectivity:
1. Bend the triggers on body-gripping traps as needed to make them selective.
2. Shape triggers to allow streamlined otters to swim through large body-gripping traps while still catching beavers, which have larger bodies.
3. Common trigger shapes include:
- Small for mink
- Small for muskrats
- Medium for raccoon and fisher
- Large for beaver and otter
4. Traps set with triggers on the bottom reduce pelt damage to the upper part of the pelt.
5. For beavers, use large triggers; for otters, adjust or cut short triggers as needed.

Use in Water Sets:
1. Select the appropriate trap: Choose a body-gripping trap of the correct size for the target animal (e.g., muskrat or mink).
2. Place the trap strategically: Position the trap at the mouth of the pocket if the animal doesn’t want to go all the way inside, or place it well inside the pocket to avoid interference from dogs.
3. Ensure proper water depth: Make sure that the water is deep enough to keep the trapped animal submerged and prevent it from breathing above water.
4. Use appropriate bait: Use bait or lures that are effective for the target species, but avoid meat or fish if there is a risk of dog interference.
5. Check traps regularly: Monitor the trap frequently to ensure that it is functioning properly and to minimize stress on captured animals.

Using Stabilizers:
1. Select a suitable stabilizer that can be used with body-gripping traps.
2. Attach the stabilizer to the trap in such a way that it supports the trap without interfering with its function.
3. Ensure that the stabilizer is placed inside the springs of the jaws so it does not interfere with the closing mechanism.
4. Use sticks or poles to stabilize body-gripping traps in channels or in front of dens.
5. Securely fasten any additional supports or crosspoles above the ice or water to prevent loss of the trap.
6. Monitor the trap regularly and check it frequently to ensure it remains functional and safe.

Safety Notes:
• States often restrict the use of body-gripping traps on land to smaller sizes.
• These traps must be used carefully to avoid harm to non-target animals.
• Large body-gripping traps are most often set under water. You can drown or die from hypothermia if you get caught in a large trap set underwater.
• Always ensure that the trap is properly secured in its location to prevent loss or theft.
• Follow local regulations regarding the use of body-gripping traps and ensure stabilizers are made from strong, durable materials that can withstand ice pressure or water conditions.

Foothold Trap Procedures (1) -

Set, Release, and Bed a Coilspring Foothold Trap Safely
Reference Source: Student manual 2005
To set, release, and bed a coilspring foothold trap safely, follow these comprehensive steps:

### Setting the Trap:
1. Prepare the trap: Ensure that the trap is clean and free of any debris or obstructions.
2. Position your hands: Place the...
To set, release, and bed a coilspring foothold trap safely, follow these comprehensive steps:

### Setting the Trap:
1. Prepare the trap: Ensure that the trap is clean and free of any debris or obstructions.
2. Position your hands: Place the palm of each hand on one of the springs.
3. Compress the springs: Press down evenly on both levers at the same time until the jaws open.
4. Hold the jaws open: Once the jaws are open, you can hold them in place with the palm and thumb of one hand.
5. Set the dog: Using the thumb on your free hand, set the dog in the notch of the pan.
6. Check placement: Release a little pressure on the jaws to make certain it is firmly in place.
7. Hold the trap securely: Hold the dog down with one thumb, then raise the free jaw and put your fingers below the jaw and the pan, holding the trap by the base plate.
8. Final positioning: Holding the pan up, put the fingers of both hands under the jaws and the pan, and set the trap in place.

### Releasing the Trap:
1. Approach the trap: Approach the trap from the side to avoid triggering it.
2. Inspect the trap: Ensure that the trap is not set and that the jaws are open.
3. Use proper tools: If the trap is set, use a safety gripper or setting tongs to release the springs.
4. Release the spring pressure: Carefully depress the levers until the jaws open fully.
5. Remove any caught animal: If an animal is caught in the trap, use appropriate tools and techniques to free it without causing harm.
6. Reset the trap: After releasing the trap, reset it properly for future use.

### Bedding the Trap:
1. Dig a shallow hole: Slightly larger than the trap and deep enough to put the trap just below ground level.
2. Drive stake(s): Use steel stakes as needed for anchoring, following the guidelines provided in the trap anchoring procedure.
3. Sift loose dirt into the bottom of the hole:
4. Press the set trap into the bottom of the hole: Ensure it is level or slightly below ground level.
5. Use the 4-point system to make sure it doesnʼt wobble:
- Press on the loose jaw
- Press on the other jaw
- Press on a lever
- Press on the other lever
6. Pack dirt around the outside of the trap: Ensure stability.
7. If the trap is wobbly at any point, pack more dirt under that area and repeat the 4-point check.

Important safety considerations:
• Always wear appropriate protective gear when handling traps.
• Always have an instructor or experienced trapper present when learning how to release a trap safely.
• Practice with your instructor until you can do it correctly.
• Never attempt to release a trap without proper tools and training.
• When working with large body-gripping traps, always carry a length of rope for safety.

Safety Procedures (1) -

Safe Use of Setting Tongs and Safety Tools When Setting Body-Gripping Traps
Reference Source: Student manual 2005
To safely set body-gripping traps (especially larger sizes like 220 and above), follow these steps:

1. Prepare the trap: Ensure that the trap is clean and free of any debris or obstructions.
2. Use setting tongs: Always use setting tongs to...
To safely set body-gripping traps (especially larger sizes like 220 and above), follow these steps:

1. Prepare the trap: Ensure that the trap is clean and free of any debris or obstructions.
2. Use setting tongs: Always use setting tongs to handle the trap and avoid direct contact with the springs.
3. Position the tongs: Place the setting tongs on the spring levers of the trap.
4. Compress the springs: Use the leverage provided by the tongs to compress the springs until the jaws open.
5. Secure with a safety hook or gripper: Once the jaws are open, secure the trap with a safety hook or Conibear™ safety gripper to prevent it from firing shut while you finish your set.
6. Install safety latches: Use safety latches on the trap to prevent accidental activation.
7. Check placement: Ensure that the trap is properly positioned and that all components are securely fastened.
8. Reset the trap: After setting the trap, reset it for future use.

Important Safety Considerations:
• Always keep setting tongs within reach when using large body-gripping traps.
• Use a Conibear™ safety gripper to keep larger traps from firing shut while you are finishing your set.
• Practice with an instructor or experienced trapper.
• These tools help reduce the risk of injury from the trap's springs.
• Always follow local regulations and guidelines for safe trapping practices.

Dirt-Hole Traps (1) -

Create a Dirt-Hole Set for Fox or Coyote Trapping
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Dirt-Hole Set Procedure

1. Select a clump of grass or other natural feature to serve as the backing for your set.

2. Dig a hole that slants back under the backing, and put the dirt in your sifter.

3. Dig a bed for the trap in...
Dirt-Hole Set Procedure

1. Select a clump of grass or other natural feature to serve as the backing for your set.

2. Dig a hole that slants back under the backing, and put the dirt in your sifter.

3. Dig a bed for the trap in front of the hole so the trap center will be about:
- 7 inches from the hole for foxes
- 12 inches from the hole for coyotes

4. Stake the trap down in the middle of the bed.

5. Set the trap and place it in the bed so that it is slightly below ground level.

6. Put a cover on the pan and sift dirt over the top to conceal the trap.

7. Place bait (about the size of a golf ball) in the hole, and cover it with light vegetation to hide it from birds of prey.

8. Apply lure to the back edge of the hole.

9. Spray fox or coyote urine on the backing using a squirt bottle. Ensure that no bait, lure, or urine gets on the trap bed.

10. Use bait such as covered meat or fish to attract the coyote.
11. Check the trap regularly for any signs of activity or capture.
dirt-hole set, fox trapping, coyote trapping, trap setting, bait placement, lure application

Cable Device Maintenance (1) -

Treat Cable Devices Prior to Use
Standard Source: Student manual 2005
Reasons for treating cable devices before use:

• To remove undesirable odors.
• To add natural scent to the device so that the animal does not become suspicious.

Procedure:

1. Prepare the boiling solution: Use **4 tablespoons...
Reasons for treating cable devices before use:

• To remove undesirable odors.
• To add natural scent to the device so that the animal does not become suspicious.

Procedure:

1. Prepare the boiling solution: Use 4 tablespoons of baking soda for every 12 sets of cable devices, along with enough water to keep the devices covered during boiling.

2. Boil for one hour: Ensure that the cable devices are fully submerged in the solution and boiled for one hour.

3. Add more water after boiling: After boiling, add more water to the container until it overflows. This helps drain the scum off the top and prevents re-contaminating the cable devices with oil when lifting them out.

4. Optional: Use logwood crystals for a darker appearance: Some trappers boil cable devices a second time with a few logwood crystals to achieve a darker color. However, avoid making the devices too dark, as they may become more visible to animals.

5. Alternative natural scent method: Instead of logwood crystals, you can use bark, moss, plant leaves, or spruce needles collected from your trapping areas in the boiling water. This will darken the cable devices and add a natural scent.
cable devices, boiling solution, baking soda, logwood crystals, natural scent, odor removal

Angling Techniques (1) -

Catch Sunfish and Redfin Using Light Tackle and Natural Bait
Reference Source: The Household Cyclopedia
Procedure for Catching Sunfish:
1. Locate shallow water areas where sunfish are commonly found.
2. Use a short rod, light line with float, and small Kirby hook for optimal results.
3. Employ natural baits such as grasshoppers, crickets, or young...
Procedure for Catching Sunfish:
1. Locate shallow water areas where sunfish are commonly found.
2. Use a short rod, light line with float, and small Kirby hook for optimal results.
3. Employ natural baits such as grasshoppers, crickets, or young bees.
4. Fish during the months of August and September when sunfish are at their largest.
5. Artificial flies can also be used effectively to catch sunfish.

Procedure for Catching Redfin:
1. Locate cold-water brooks in the northern and middle portions of the United States where redfin are commonly found.
2. Use very light tackle with a small, long-shanked Kirby hook for optimal results.
3. Employ red worms as bait for catching redfin.
4. Fish during the spring months when redfin are most active.
5. Redfin seldom exceed 7 or 8 inches in length and are excellent pan-fish.
sunfish, redfin, light tackle, natural bait, fishing, Kirby hook, red worms
